I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare it with each candidate formula.

**GT numerical expression:**
`-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*x*(0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
`-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*0.0552411020531317*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 1.1056075693807*x - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

= `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 0.0610788418898*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 2.2112151387614*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

So the GT has these terms:
1. A constant times `x` (≈ -2.2112)
2. A constant times `sin(t)` (≈ 0.3508)
3. A constant times `v**3` (≈ -0.0230)
4. A constant times `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)` (≈ -0.0611)

Note: `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2) = cos(-π/2 + t)`, so `c1*cos(c2 + t)` with `c2 = -π/2` gives `c1*sin(t)`.

The GT is essentially: `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

Now let me check **Candidate 33**: `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

This is exactly the form of the GT! Setting:
- c0 = -2.2112151387614
- c1 = 0.350781823399691, c2 = -π/2
- c3 = -0.0230405406738805
- c4 = -0.0610788418898

This matches perfectly.

Let me also verify **Candidate 50**: `c0*x + c1*cos(c2*t + c3) + c4*v**3 + c5*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

Setting c2 = 1 makes `cos(t + c3)`, which is the same as candidate 33. This also matches.

Several other candidates contain the core terms of candidate 33 plus additional terms that can be zeroed out:

- **Candidate 15** (`+ c5*x + c6`): c5 absorbs into c0, c6=0. Matches.
- **Candidate 16** (`+ c5`): c5=0. Matches.
- **Candidate 22** (`+ c5*v`): c5=0. Matches.

- **Candidate 53** (`+ c5*t + c6`): c5=0, c6=0. Matches.

And many others where extra terms can be set to zero.

+ c5*x*sin(c6*t + c7)", "c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*t**c4 + c5*v**3 + c6*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)", "c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c5*v*cos(c6*t)", "c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*x*(0.0552411020531317*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333 + 1) - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
`-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 1.1056075693807*0.0552411020531317*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 1.1056075693807*x - 1.1056075693807*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

= `-0.0230405406738805*v**3 - 0.0610812*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) - 2.2112151387614*x + 0.350781823399691*sin(t)`

So GT has these basis functions:
1. `x` (linear)
2. `sin(t)` (equivalently `cos(t + c)` with appropriate phase shift)
3. `v**3`
4. `x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`

That's exactly 4 terms. Note that `cos(c2 + t)` can equal `sin(t)` when `c2 = π/2`.

Now I'll check each candidate:

**Candidate 33:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
This has exactly the 4 basis functions needed. Set c2 = π/2 to get sin(t). ✓

**Candidate 15:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c5*x + c6`
Extra terms `c5*x` merges with `c0*x`, and `c6` is a constant. Set c6=0. This works. ✓

**Candidate 16:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**(1/3) + c5`
Set c5=0. ✓

**Candidate 50:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2*t + c3) + c4*v**3 + c5*x*Abs(v)**(1/3)`
Set c2=1, c3=π/2. Same as GT. ✓

**Candidate 32:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v**3 + c4*x*Abs(v)**c5`
Set c5=1/3. ✓

Now let me systematically check all others. The key question for each is: can the extra terms be zeroed out or absorbed?

- **Candidate 4:** extra `c3 + c6*v` → set c3=0, c6=0. ✓

- **Candidate 44:** extra `c5*v*x**2` → set c5=0. ✓
- **Candidate 45:** extra `c5*v*Abs(v)` → set c5=0. ✓

- **Candidate 1:** `c5*sin(c6*log(c7*Abs(x)+1)+c8)` → set c5=0. ✓
- **Candidate 2:** `c5*log(c6*x**2+c7*v**2+1)` → set c5=0. ✓
